## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: thermomechanical constitutive modeling
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature relationship in materials, a core problem in solid mechanics and materials science. Temperature typically causes thermal softening (reduced stiffness), while strain determines the mechanical response through linear or nonlinear constitutive laws.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke's law: sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elastic stress-strain relationship)
- Temperature-dependent linear elasticity: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (1 + c1 * T) (elastic modulus varying linearly with temperature)
- Temperature-dependent elasticity (exponential softening): sigma = c0 * epsilon * exp(c1 * T) (thermal softening of elastic modulus)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (nonlinear strain hardening in plasticity)
- Ramberg-Osgood type: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2 (elastic-plastic with strain hardening)
- Johnson-Cook thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (1 + c2 * T)**c3 (combined strain hardening and thermal softening)
- Ludwik hardening with temperature: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * exp(c3 * T) (power-law hardening with exponential thermal softening)
- Voce hardening: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) (saturating stress-strain curve)
- Voce with temperature dependence: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) * (1 + c2 * T) (saturating hardening with thermal effect)
- Polynomial stress-strain: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (higher-order elastic or hyperelastic response)
- Hyperbolic sine flow stress: sigma = c0 * T * arcsinh(c1 * epsilon) (high-temperature creep/flow behavior)
- Neo-Hookean type: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * epsilon**3) * exp(c2 * T) (hyperelastic with thermal dependence)
- Thermal softening power law: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * T**c2 (power-law coupling of strain and temperature)
- Swift hardening: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 (shifted power-law hardening with pre-strain)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Thermal softening at high temperature → multiplicative factor (1 - c*T/T_melt) or exp(-c*T) reducing stress magnitude
- Strain hardening saturation → (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) form indicating stress approaching a plateau at large strains
- Multiplicative decomposition of strain and temperature effects → sigma = f(epsilon) * g(T), separable contributions
- Concave-up stress-strain at small strains transitioning to concave-down → combination of linear and power-law terms with exponent < 1
- Temperature-dependent elastic modulus → E(T) = c0 + c1*T or c0*exp(c1*T) as prefactor to strain terms
- Strain rate-independent plasticity → power-law or logarithmic dependence on strain without time derivatives
- Phase transition or material instability → non-monotonic temperature dependence, e.g., polynomial in T with sign changes
- Rubber-like hyperelasticity → odd powers of strain (epsilon, epsilon**3) reflecting symmetric tension-compression behavior

No T dependence at all. **No match.**
